## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration depends on position (restoring force, possibly nonlinear), velocity (damping), and possibly time (external driving). Classical nonlinear oscillator models like Duffing, van der Pol, and driven oscillators are the primary candidates.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force, c0 < 0)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Van der Pol form 2: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Mathieu-Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * cos(c3 * t) (parametric + nonlinear)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric + cubic restoring)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve oscillator symmetry; even powers (x²) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-position coupling terms like x²·v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators (van der Pol type)
- Periodic time dependence (sin/cos of t) in acceleration indicates external driving forces; look for harmonic or multi-frequency driving
- Product terms x·cos(c·t) indicate parametric excitation where the effective stiffness is time-modulated
- Cubic velocity terms (v³) model nonlinear drag where dissipation increases faster than linearly with speed
- If acceleration depends only on x and v (no explicit t), the system is autonomous and energy methods apply
- Sign of the cubic coefficient relative to linear term determines hardening (same sign as restoring) vs softening (opposite sign) spring behavior
- Negative linear damping combined with positive nonlinear damping (e.g., -v + x²v) produces limit cycle oscillations

- **Candidate 13**: Has `c7*x*(c8 + v)**c9` — this could expand to include `v*x` terms but not `v*x²`.
- **Candidate 41**: Has `c7*v*(c8 + t)**c9` — this is v times a function of t, not x.
- **Candidate 47**: Has `c7*v*(c8 + x)**3` — expands to `c7*v*(x³ + 3c8*x² + 3c8²*x + c8³)`, which gives `v*x³`, `v*x²`, `v*x`, `v` terms. Also has `c1*sin(c2*x + c3)` which could give `sin(x)` but NOT `v*sin(x)`.
- **Candidate 50**: Has `c7*v*(c8 + t)**c9` — v times function of t, not x.

**Candidate 47** is the most promising: `c0*v + c1*sin(c2*x + c3) + c4*sin(c5 + c6*t) + c7*v*(c8 + x)**3 + x**2 + x`

Expanding `c7*v*(c8 + x)³ = c7*v*(c8³ + 3c8²x + 3c8x² + x³)`. This gives `v*x³` which GT doesn't have. We can't set c7=0 without losing `v*x²`. So this doesn't work.

Also, GT requires `v*sin(x)` — none of the candidates have this term (they'd need `v*sin(x)` explicitly).

Since `v*sin(x)` is a linearly independent basis function that appears in GT with a non-zero coefficient, and NO candidate contains this term or any equivalent, **no candidate can match**.

Let me verify: `-0.377828837635262*v*sin(x)` is indeed present and nonzero. None of the candidates have a `v*sin(x)` term.
